class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Closing"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Closing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Medal_presentation"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Medal presentation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#List_of_Commonwealth_Games"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">List of Commonwealth Games</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#All-time_medal_table"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">All-time medal table</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#List_of_Commonwealth_sports"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">List of Commonwealth sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Participation"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Participation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Commonwealth_nations_yet_to_send_teams"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Commonwealth nations yet to send teams</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Controversies"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Controversies</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Host_city_contract"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Host city contract</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Boycotts"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Boycotts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Budget"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Budget</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Notable_competitors"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notable competitors</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_Games">History of the Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of the Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A sporting <a href="/wiki/Competition" title="Competition">competition</a> bringing together the members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> was first proposed by John Astley Cooper in 1900, when he wrote an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> suggesting a "Pan-Britannic-Pan-Anglican Contest and Festival every four years as a means of increasing goodwill and good understanding of the British Empire". John Astley Cooper Committees were formed worldwide (e.g. Australia) and helped <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin" title="Pierre de Coubertin">Pierre de Coubertin</a> to get his international <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> off the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 1911, the <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival of the Empire">Festival of the Empire</a> was held at <a href="/wiki/The_Crystal_Palace" title="The Crystal Palace">The Crystal Palace</a> in London to celebrate the <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a>. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival of the Empire">Festival of the Empire</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Empire#Inter-Empire_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival of the Empire">Inter-Empire Championships</a> were held in which teams from Australia, Canada, South Africa, and the United Kingdom competed in athletics, boxing, wrestling and swimming events.\n</p><p>Canada won the championships and was gifted a silver cup which was 2 feet 6 inch high and weighed 340 oz (9.6 kg). It was gifted by <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Lonsdale" title="Earl of Lonsdale">Lord Lonsdale</a>. However, the 1911 championships were followed by the <a href="/wiki/First_world_war" class="mw-redirect" title="First world war">first world war</a> which happened from 1914 to 1918. The organisers had lost hopes of hosting such sporting events for the empire athletes. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Melville_Marks_Robinson" title="Melville Marks Robinson">Melville Marks Robinson</a>, who went to the <a href="/wiki/1928_Summer_Olympics" title="1928 Summer Olympics">1928 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> to serve as the manager of the Canadian track and field team, strongly lobbied for the proposal of organising the first British Empire Games in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a> in 1930.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editions_of_the_Games">Editions of the Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Editions of the Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_the_20th_century">During the 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: During the 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Empire_Games">British Empire Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: British Empire Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1930_British_Empire_Games" title="1930 British Empire Games">1930&#160;British Empire&#160;Games</a>&#160;were the first of what later become known as the&#160;Commonwealth Games, and were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>, in the province of&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>&#160;in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>&#160;from August 16\xe2\x80\x9323, 1930. \n</p><p>Eleven countries sent a total of 400 athletes to the Hamilton Games. The opening and closing ceremonies as well as athletics took place at <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Wynne_Stadium" title="Ivor Wynne Stadium">Civic Stadium</a>. The participant nations were <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>. The Hamilton Games featured six sports: athletics, boxing, lawn bowls, rowing, swimming and diving and wrestling and ran at a cost of $97,973. Women competed in only the aquatic events.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Canadian triple jumper <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Smallacombe" title="Gordon Smallacombe">Gordon Smallacombe</a> won the first ever gold medal in the history of the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg/220px-SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg/330px-SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg/440px-SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1068" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SLNSW_23801_Opening_Empire_Games_Sydney_Cricket_Ground.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/1938_British_Empire_Games" title="1938 British Empire Games">1938 British Empire Games</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a>.</div></div></div><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1934_British_Empire_Games" title="1934 British Empire Games">1934 British Empire Games</a>&#160;were the second of what is now known as the&#160;Commonwealth Games, held in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. The host city was&#160;<a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, with the main venue at&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wembley_Park" title="Wembley Park">Wembley Park</a>, although the track cycling events were in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>. The 1934 Games had originally been awarded to <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, but were given to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> instead because of serious concerns about prejudice against black and Asian athletes in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.  Seventeen national teams took part, including the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> (the only Games in which they did take part) and new participants <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Jamaica" title="Colony of Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1938_British_Empire_Games" title="1938 British Empire Games">1938 British Empire Games</a>&#160;were the third&#160;<a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="British Empire Games">British Empire Games</a>, which were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. They were timed to coincide with Sydney\'s sesqui-centenary (150 years since the foundation of British settlement in Australia).&#160;Held in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">southern hemisphere</a> for the first time, the III Games opening ceremony took place at the famed <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a> in front of 40,000 spectators. Fifteen nations participated down under at the Sydney Games involving a total of 464 athletes and 43 officials. <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Fiji" title="Colony of Fiji">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Ceylon</a> made their debuts. Seven sports were featured in the Sydney Games \xe2\x80\x93 athletics, boxing, cycling, lawn bowls, rowing, swimming and diving and wrestling.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1950_British_Empire_Games" title="1950 British Empire Games">1950 British Empire Games</a>&#160;were the fourth edition and was held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> after a 12-year gap from the third edition of the games. The fourth games were originally awarded to&#160;<a href="/wiki/Montreal,_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal, Canada">Montreal, Canada</a>&#160;and were to be held in 1942 but were cancelled due to&#160;the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The opening ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Eden_Park" title="Eden Park">Eden Park</a> was attended by 40,000 spectators, while nearly 250,000 people attended the Auckland Games. Twelve countries sent a total of 590 athletes to <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Malaya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> made their first appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games">British Empire and Commonwealth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British Empire and Commonwealth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bannister_and_Landy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bannister_and_Landy.jpg/170px-Bannister_and_Landy.jpg" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bannister_and_Landy.jpg/255px-Bannister_and_Landy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Bannister_and_Landy.jpg/340px-Bannister_and_Landy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bannister_and_Landy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue in Vancouver commemorating the "Miracle Mile" between <a href="/wiki/Roger_Bannister" title="Roger Bannister">Roger Bannister</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Landy" title="John Landy">John Landy</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The fifth edition of the games, the <a href="/wiki/1954_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1954 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1954 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a>, were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. These were the first games since the name change from&#160;<a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="British Empire Games">British Empire Games</a>&#160;took effect in 1952. The fifth edition of the Games placed <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> on a world stage and featured memorable sporting moments as well as outstanding entertainment, technical innovation and cultural events. The \xe2\x80\x98Miracle Mile\xe2\x80\x99, as it became known, saw both the gold medallist, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Bannister" title="Roger Bannister">Roger Bannister</a> of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and silver medallist <a href="/wiki/John_Landy" title="John Landy">John Landy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, run sub-four minute races in an event that was televised live across the world for the first time. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rhodesia" title="Northern Rhodesia">Northern Rhodesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> made their debuts and both performed well, winning eight and six medals respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg/220px-1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg/330px-1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg/440px-1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="975" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1958_Commonwealth_Games_3d_Stamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>3pence British stamp with theme of&#160;<a href="/wiki/1958_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1958_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a> were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>.&#160;The sixth edition of the games marked the largest sporting event ever held in Wales and it was the smallest country ever to host a British Empire and Commonwealth Games. <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> had to wait 12 years longer than originally scheduled to become host of the Games, as the 1946 event was cancelled because of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The Cardiff Games introduced the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Queen\'s Baton Relay</a>, which has been conducted as a prelude to every British Empire and Commonwealth Games ever since. Thirty-five nations sent a total of 1,122 athletes and 228 officials to the Cardiff Games and 23 countries and dependencies won medals, including for the first time, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Colony" title="Kenya Colony">Kenya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1962_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1962 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1962 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. Thirty-five countries sent a total of 863 athletes and 178 officials to <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> was among the medal winners for the first time, while <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">British Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Papua_and_New_Guinea" title="Territory of Papua and New Guinea">Papua and New Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">St Lucia</a> all made their inaugural Games appearances. <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Aden" title="Colony of Aden">Aden</a> also competed by special invitation. <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Malaya</a> competed for the last time before taking part in 1966 under the <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysian flag">Malaysian flag</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Rhodesia_and_Nyasaland" title="Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland">Rhodesia and Nyasaland</a> competed in the Games as an entity for the first and only time.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1966_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1966 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1966 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston, Jamaica</a>. This was the first time that the Games had been held outside the so-called&#160;<a href="/wiki/White_Dominion" class="mw-redirect" title="White Dominion">White Dominions</a>. Thirty-four nations (including <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_South_Arabia" title="Federation of South Arabia">South Arabia</a>) competed in the <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a> Games sending a total of 1,316 athletes and officials.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Commonwealth_Games">British Commonwealth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: British Commonwealth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1970_British_Commonwealth_Games" title="1970 British Commonwealth Games">1970 British Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.&#160;This was the first time the name&#160;<a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth Games">British Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;was adopted, the first time&#160;<a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric units</a>&#160;rather than&#160;<a href="/wiki/Imperial_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial unit">imperial units</a>&#160;were used in events,  the first time the games were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and also the first time that HM Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> attended in her capacity as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1974_British_Commonwealth_Games" title="1974 British Commonwealth Games">1974 British&#160;Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. The Games were officially named <i>"the friendly games"</i>.&#160;Following the <a href="/wiki/1972_Munich_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="1972 Munich attack">massacre of Israeli athletes</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Munich Olympics</a>, the tenth games at <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a> were the first <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> to place the safety of participants and spectators as its uppermost requirement. Security guards surrounded the athlete\xe2\x80\x99s village and there was an exceptionally high-profile police presence. Only 22 countries succeeded in winning medals from the total haul of 374 medals on offer, but first time winners included <a href="/wiki/Western_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Samoa">Western Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_Games">Commonwealth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Commonwealth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1978_Commonwealth_Games" title="1978 Commonwealth Games">1978&#160;Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. This event was the first to bear the current day name of the Commonwealth Games and also marked a new high as almost 1,500 athletes from 46 countries took part. They were boycotted by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> in protest of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>\'s sporting contacts with <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>-era South Africa, as well as by <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> in protest of alleged Canadian hostility towards the government of <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">Idi Amin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MacintoshHawes1994_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacintoshHawes1994-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg/220px-Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg/330px-Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg/440px-Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2999" data-file-height="1958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_Games_Opening_Ceremony_-_Brisbane_1982.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982 Commonwealth Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982&#160;Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. Forty-six nations participated in the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> Games with a new record total of 1,583 athletes and 571 officials. As hosts, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> headed the medal table leading the way ahead of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> respectively. <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> made its first appearance at the Games, having earlier competed as Southern Rhodesia and as part of <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Rhodesia_and_Nyasaland" title="Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland">Rhodesia and Nyasaland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1986_Commonwealth_Games" title="1986 Commonwealth Games">1986 Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and were the second Games to be held in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. Participation at the <a href="/wiki/1986_Commonwealth_Games" title="1986 Commonwealth Games">1986 Games</a> was affected by a boycott by 32 African, Asian and Caribbean nations in protest of British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret Thatcher&#39;s">Margaret Thatcher\'s</a> refusal to condemn sporting contacts of apartheid era South Africa in 1985, but the Games rebounded and continued to grow thereafter. Twenty-six nations did attend the second <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> Games and sent a total of 1,662 athletes and 461 officials.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1990_Commonwealth_Games" title="1990 Commonwealth Games">1990 Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. It was the fourteenth&#160;Commonwealth Games, the third to be hosted by <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_at_the_Commonwealth_Games" title="New Zealand at the Commonwealth Games">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>\xe2\x80\x99s second. A new record of 55 nations participated in the second <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> Games sending 2,826 athletes and officials.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Pakistan returned to the Commonwealth in 1989 after withdrawing in 1972, and competed in the 1990 Games after an absence of twenty years.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1994_Commonwealth_Games" title="1994 Commonwealth Games">1994 Commonwealth Games</a> were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, the fourth to take place in Canada. The games marked&#160;<a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>\'s return to the Commonwealth Games following the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>&#160;era, and over 30 years since the country last competed in the&#160;<a href="/wiki/1958_Commonwealth_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="1958 Commonwealth Games">Games in 1958</a>. <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> made its Commonwealth Games debut. It was also&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>\'s last appearance at the games before the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">transfer of sovereignty</a>&#160;from Britain to&#160;<a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. Sixty-three nations sent 2,557 athletes and 914 officials.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998 Commonwealth Games</a>&#160;were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. For the first time in its 68-year history, the Commonwealth Games were held in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. The sixteenth games were also the first Games to feature team sports - an overwhelming success that added large numbers to both participant and TV audience numbers. A new record of 70 countries sent a total of 5,065 athletes and officials to the <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a> Games. The top five countries in the medal standing were <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> also achieved an impressive haul of three gold medals. <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> debuted.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_the_21st_century">During the 21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: During the 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a> were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. The 2002 Games were to be hosted in England to coincide with the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II</a>, head of the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>. In terms of sports and events, the 2002 Games were until the 2010 edition the largest Commonwealth Games in history featuring 281 events across 17 sports. The final medal tally was led by <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, followed by host <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The 2002 Commonwealth Games had set a new benchmark for hosting the Commonwealth Games and for cities wishing to bid for them with a heavy emphasis on legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MSC,_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg/220px-MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg/330px-MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg/440px-MSC%2C_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MSC,_2006_Commonwealth_Games.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Athletics at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> (MCG) during the <a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games" title="2006 Commonwealth Games">2006 Commonwealth Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The&#160;<a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games" title="2006 Commonwealth Games">2006&#160;Commonwealth Games</a> were held in&#160;<a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, Victoria, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. The only difference between the <a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games" title="2006 Commonwealth Games">2006 games</a> and the&#160;<a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 games</a>&#160;was the absence of&#160;<a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, which withdrew from the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. For the first time in the history of the Games the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Queen\'s Baton</a> visited every single Commonwealth nation and territory taking part in the Games, a journey of 180,000&#160;km (112,500 miles). Over 4000 athletes took part in the sporting competitions. Again the Top 3 on the medal table is <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. The Games cost $11&#160;billion and are the most expensive Commonwealth Games ever. It was the first time that the Commonwealth Games were held in India,also the first time that a Commonwealth Republic hosted the games and the second time they were held in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> after&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> in&#160;<a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998</a>.&#160;A total of 6,081 athletes from 71&#160;<a href="/wiki/The_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="The Commonwealth">Commonwealth nations and dependencies</a>&#160;competed in 21 sports and 272 events. The final&#160;<a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games_medal_table" title="2010 Commonwealth Games medal table">medal tally</a>&#160;was led by&#160;<a href="/wiki/Australia_at_the_2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="Australia at the 2010 Commonwealth Games">Australia</a>. The host nation <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> achieved its&#160;<a href="/wiki/India_at_the_2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="India at the 2010 Commonwealth Games">best performance ever in any sporting event</a>, finishing second overall.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> made its Games debut.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. It was the largest&#160;<a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a>&#160;ever held in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> with around 4,950 athletes from 71 different nations and territories competing in 18 different sports, outranking the&#160;<a href="/wiki/1970_British_Commonwealth_Games" title="1970 British Commonwealth Games">1970</a>&#160;and&#160;<a href="/wiki/1986_Commonwealth_Games" title="1986 Commonwealth Games">1986</a>&#160;Commonwealth Games in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, capital city of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Usain_Bolt" title="Usain Bolt">Usain Bolt</a> competed in the&#160;<a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="Athletics at the 2014 Commonwealth Games">4\xc3\x97100 metres relay</a>&#160;of the&#160;<a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</a> and set a&#160;<a href="/wiki/List_of_Commonwealth_Games_records_in_athletics#Men.27s_records" title="List of Commonwealth Games records in athletics">Commonwealth Games record</a> with his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Games received acclaim for their organisation, attendance, and the public enthusiasm of the people of Scotland, with&#160;<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a>&#160;chief executive Mike Hooper hailing them as "the standout games in the history of the movement".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018 Commonwealth Games</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the fifth time Australia hosted the Games. There were an equal number of events for men and women, the first time in history that a major&#160;<a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a>&#160;had equality in terms of events.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2022_Commonwealth_Games" title="2022 Commonwealth Games">2022 Commonwealth Games</a> will be held in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. They will be the third Commonwealth Games to be hosted in England following <a href="/wiki/1934_British_Empire_Games" title="1934 British Empire Games">London 1934</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">Manchester 2002</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The three nations to have hosted the Commonwealth Games the most times are <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (5), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (4) and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (3). Furthermore, six editions have taken place in the countries within the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> (2) and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> (1)), twice in Asia (<a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (1) and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (1)) and once in the Caribbean (<a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> (1)).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraplegic_Games">Paraplegic Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Paraplegic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">Commonwealth Paraplegic Games</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg/220px-1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg/330px-1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg/440px-1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2904" data-file-height="2098" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games_Competitors_Team_Photograph.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Athletes of the <a href="/wiki/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1962 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1962 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Commonwealth Paraplegic Games were an international, <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> involving athletes with a disability from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth countries</a>. The event was sometimes referred to as the Paraplegic Empire Games and British Commonwealth Paraplegic Games. Athletes were generally those with <a href="/wiki/Spinal_injuries" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinal injuries">spinal injuries</a> or <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a>. The event was first held in 1962 and disestablished in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The Games were held in the country hosting the Commonwealth Games for able-bodied athletes. The countries that had hosted the Commonwealth Paraplegic Games were Australia, Jamaica, Scotland and New Zealand in <a href="/wiki/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1962 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1966 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1970_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1970 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1970</a> and <a href="/wiki/1974_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1974 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1974</a> respectively. Six countries \xe2\x80\x94 Australia, England, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> \xe2\x80\x94 had been represented at all Commonwealth Paraplegic Games. Australia and England had been the top-ranking nation two times each: <a href="/wiki/1962_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1962 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1974_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1974 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1974</a> and <a href="/wiki/1966_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1966 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1970_Commonwealth_Paraplegic_Games" title="1970 Commonwealth Paraplegic Games">1970</a> respectively.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inclusion_of_Para-sports">Inclusion of Para-sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Inclusion of Para-sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Athletes with a disability were then first included in exhibition events at the <a href="/wiki/1994_Commonwealth_Games" title="1994 Commonwealth Games">1994 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and, at the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, they were included as full members of their national teams, making them the first fully inclusive international multi-sport games. This meant that results were included in the medal count.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 2007 General Assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a> (CGF) at <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Paralympic_Committee" title="International Paralympic Committee">International Paralympic Committee</a> (IPC) and CGF signed a co-operative agreement to ensure a formal institutional relationship between the two bodies and secure the future participation of elite athletes with a disability (EAD) in future Commonwealth Games.\n</p><p>IPC President <a href="/wiki/Philip_Craven" title="Philip Craven">Philip Craven</a> said during the General Assembly:\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style=";"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x9cWe look forward to working with CGF to develop the possibilities of athletes with a disability at the Commonwealth Games and within the Commonwealth. This partnership will help to galvanize Paralympic sports development in Commonwealth countries/territories and seek to create and promote greater opportunities in sport for athletes with a disability.\xe2\x80\x9d</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 IPC President <a href="/wiki/Sir_Philip_Craven" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Philip Craven">Sir Philip Craven</a></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The co-operation agreement outlined the strong partnership between the IPC and the CGF. It recognized the IPC as the organization for overseeing the co-ordination and delivery of the Commonwealth Games EAD sports programme and committed both organizations to work together in supporting the growth of the Paralympic and Commonwealth Games Movements.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Winter_Games">Winter Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Winter Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Winter_Games" title="Commonwealth Winter Games">Commonwealth Winter Games</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StMoritz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/StMoritz.jpg/220px-StMoritz.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/StMoritz.jpg/330px-StMoritz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/StMoritz.jpg/440px-StMoritz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="738" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StMoritz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, the venue for all three Games from 1958-66</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Winter_Games" title="Commonwealth Winter Games">Commonwealth Winter Games</a> were a <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> comprising <a href="/wiki/Winter_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter sports">winter sports</a>, last held in 1966. Three editions of the Games have been staged. The Winter Games were designed as a counterbalance to the Commonwealth Games, which focuses on summer sports, to accompany the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a>. The winter Games were founded by <a href="/wiki/T.D._Richardson" class="mw-redirect" title="T.D. Richardson">T.D. Richardson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Semanticus-Richardson_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Semanticus-Richardson-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The 1958 Commonwealth Winter Games were held in <a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and was the inaugural games for the winter edition.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The 1962 Games were also held in St. Moritz, complementing the <a href="/wiki/1962_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1962 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1962 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Western_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Perth, Western Australia">Perth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, and the 1966 event was held in St. Moritz as well, following which the idea was discontinued.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_Games">Youth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Youth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Youth_Games" title="Commonwealth Youth Games">Commonwealth Youth Games</a></div>\n<p>The Commonwealth Youth Games are an international <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> organized by the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a>. The games are held every four years with the current Commonwealth Games format. The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a> discussed the idea of a Millennium Commonwealth Youth Games in 1997. In 1998 the concept was agreed on for the purpose of providing a Commonwealth multi-sport event for young people born in the calendar year 1986 or later. The first version was held in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> from 10 to 14 August <a href="/wiki/2000_Commonwealth_Youth_Games" title="2000 Commonwealth Youth Games">2000</a>. The age limitation of the athletes is 14 to 18.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_Games_Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Commonwealth Games Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Shopping_002_(6166876525)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-London_Shopping_002_%286166876525%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Shopping_002_(6166876525)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">CGF</a> at the Commonwealth House (centre) in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Commonwealth Games Federation (CGF) is the international organisation responsible for the direction and control of the Commonwealth Games and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Youth_Games" title="Commonwealth Youth Games">Commonwealth Youth Games</a>, and is the foremost authority in matters relating to the games.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The Commonwealth House in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> hosts the headquarters of CGF.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Commonwealth House also hosts the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commonwealth_Society" title="Royal Commonwealth Society">Royal Commonwealth Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Local_Government_Forum" title="Commonwealth Local Government Forum">Commonwealth Local Government Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Commonwealth Games Movement is made of three major elements:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_international_sport_federations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of international sport federations">International Federations</a> (IFs) are the <a href="/wiki/Sport_governing_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport governing body">governing bodies</a> that supervise a sport at an international level. For example, the International Basketball Federation (<a href="/wiki/FIBA" title="FIBA">FIBA</a>) is the international governing body for basketball.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Category:Commonwealth_Games_Associations" title="Category:Commonwealth Games Associations">Commonwealth Games Associations</a> (CGAs) represent and regulate the Commonwealth Games Movement within each country. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_England" title="Commonwealth Games England">Commonwealth Games England</a> (CGE) is the CGA of England. There are currently 70 CGAs recognised by the CGF.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Organising Committees for the Commonwealth Games (OCCWGs) are temporary committees responsible for the organisation of each Commonwealth Games. OCCWGs are dissolved after each Games once the final report is delivered to the CGF.</li></ul>\n<p>English is the official language of the Commonwealth. The other language used at each Commonwealth Games is the language of the host country (or languages, if a country has more than one official language apart from English). Every proclamation (such as the announcement of each country during the parade of nations in the opening ceremony) is spoken in these two (or more) languages, or the main depending on whether the host country is an English speaking country.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Queen.27s_Baton_Relay"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Queen\'s_Baton_Relay">Queen\'s Baton Relay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Queen&#039;s Baton Relay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Queen\'s Baton Relay</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg/220px-Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg/330px-Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg/440px-Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilston_St.-Garrick_St._-_geograph.org.uk_-_536739.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2002 <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay#Manchester_2002" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Queen\'s Jubilee Baton Relay</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Queen\'s Baton Relay, is a relay around the world held prior to the beginning of the Commonwealth Games. The Baton carries a message from the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a>, currently Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>. The Relay traditionally begins at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> as a part of the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Day" title="Commonwealth Day">Commonwealth Day</a> festivities. The Queen entrusts the baton to the first relay runner. At the Opening Ceremony of the Games, the final relay runner hands the baton back to the Queen or her representative, who reads the message aloud to officially open the Games. The Queen\'s Baton Relay is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Torch_Relay" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Torch Relay">Olympic Torch Relay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RelayTradition_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RelayTradition-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Relay was introduced at the <a href="/wiki/1958_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1958 British Empire and Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>. Up until, and including, the <a href="/wiki/1994_Commonwealth_Games" title="1994 Commonwealth Games">1994 Games</a>, the Relay only went through <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and the host nation. The Relay for the <a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998 Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> was the first to travel to other nations of the Commonwealth. The <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay#Gold_Coast_2018" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Gold Coast 2018 Queen\xe2\x80\x99s Baton Relay</a> was the longest in Commonwealth Games history. Covering 230,000&#160;km over 388 days, the Baton made its way through the six Commonwealth regions of Africa, the Americas, the Caribbean, Europe, Asia and Oceania. For the first time, the Queen\'s Baton was presented at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Youth_Games" title="Commonwealth Youth Games">Commonwealth Youth Games</a> during its <a href="/wiki/2017_Commonwealth_Youth_Games" title="2017 Commonwealth Youth Games">sixth edition</a> in 2017 which were held in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremonies">Ceremonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ceremonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening">Opening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Opening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG/220px-Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG/330px-Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG/440px-Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comm_Games_2006_finale.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games" title="2006 Commonwealth Games">2006 Commonwealth Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Various elements frame the opening ceremony of the Commonwealth Games. This ceremony takes place before the events have occurred. The ceremony typically starts with the hoisting of the host country\'s flag and a performance of its national anthem. The flag of the Commonwealth Games Federation, flag of the last hosting nation and the next hosting nation are also hosted during the opening ceremony. The host nation then presents artistic displays of music, singing, dance and theatre representative of its culture. The artistic presentations have grown in scale and complexity as successive hosts attempt to provide a ceremony that outlasts its predecessor\'s in terms of memorability. The opening ceremony of the Delhi Games reportedly cost $70&#160;million, with much of the cost incurred in the artistic segment.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the artistic portion of the ceremony, the athletes parade into the stadium grouped by nation. The last hosting nation is traditionally the first nation to enter. Nations then enter the stadium alphabetical or continental wise with the host country\'s athletes being the last to enter. Speeches are given, formally opening the Games. Finally, the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Baton_Relay" title="Queen&#39;s Baton Relay">Queen\'s Baton</a> is brought into the stadium and passed on until it reaches the final baton carrier, often a successful Commonwealth athlete from the host nation, who hands it over to the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a> or their representative.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closing">Closing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Closing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg/220px-Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg/330px-Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg/440px-Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1464" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_Games_closing_ceremony_picture.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Closing ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The closing ceremony of the Commonwealth Games takes place after all sporting events have concluded. Flag-bearers from each participating country enter the stadium, followed by the athletes who enter together, without any national distinction. The president of the organizing committee and the CGF president make their closing speeches and the Games are officially closed. The CGF president also speaks about the conduct of the games. The mayor of the city that organized the Games transfers the CGF flag to the president of the CGF, who then passes it on to the mayor of the city hosting the next Commonwealth Games. The next host nation then also briefly introduces itself with artistic displays of dance and theater representative of its culture. Many great artists and singers had performed at the ceremonies of the Commonwealth Games.\n</p><p>At the closing ceremony of every Commonwealth Games the CGF President makes an award and presents a trophy to one athlete who has competed with particular distinction and honour both in terms of athletic performance and overall contribution to his or her team. Athletes are nominated by their Commonwealth Games Association at the end of the final day of competition and the winner is selected by a panel comprising the CGF President and representatives from each of the six Commonwealth Regions. The \xe2\x80\x98<a href="/wiki/David_Dixon_Award" title="David Dixon Award">David Dixon Award</a>\xe2\x80\x99 as it is called was introduced in <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">Manchester 2002</a>, after the late David Dixon, former Honorary Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">CGF</a>, in honour of his monumental contribution to Commonwealth sport for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_presentation">Medal presentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Medal presentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A medal ceremony is held after each event is concluded. The winner, second and third-place competitors or teams stand on top of a three-tiered rostrum to be awarded their respective medals. After the medals are given out by a CGF member, the national flags of the three medallists are raised while the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of the gold medallist\'s country plays. Volunteering citizens of the host country also act as hosts during the medal ceremonies, as they aid the officials who present the medals and act as flag-bearers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" href="/wiki/Festival_of_Empire#Inter-Empire_Championships" title="Festival of Empire">Inter-Empire Championships</a> held in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> is seen as a precursor to the modern Commonwealth Games, but is not normally considered an official edition of the Games themselves. Also, the United Kingdom competed as one country, unlike the Commonwealth Games today when they compete as <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Canada topped the medal table by winning 4 events.</i><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" style="font-weight:bold">8891</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Commonwealth_sports">List of Commonwealth sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: List of Commonwealth sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_sports" title="Commonwealth Games sports">Commonwealth Games sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_records" title="Commonwealth Games records">Commonwealth Games records</a></div>\n<p>There are a total of 22 sports (with three multi-disciplinary sports) and a further seven <a href="/wiki/Para-sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Para-sports">para-sports</a> which are approved by the Commonwealth Games Federation. Core sports must be included on each programme. A number of optional sports may be picked by the host nation, which may include some team sports such as <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>.\n</p>\n<center>\n<table 2010\xe2\x80\x93present\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></center>\n<p>In 2015, the Commonwealth Games Federation agreed large changes to the programme which increased the number of core sports, whilst removing a number of optionals, those removed are listed below.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table Games Federation but which are deemed to need expansion; host nations may not pick these sports for their programme until the Federation\'s requirements are fulfilled.<sup id="cite_ref-Sports_61-0" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Participation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Only six teams have attended every Commonwealth Games: Australia, Canada, England, New Zealand, Scotland and Wales. Australia has been the highest scoring team for thirteen games, England for seven and Canada for one.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder"
