href="#endnote_n23">23</a></sup></td>\n<td>1982, 1990\xe2\x80\x932002\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></center>\n<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ol><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n1"><b><a href="#ref_n1">^</a></b></span>  Aden later joined South Arabia in 1963 and departed the Commonwealth in 1968.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n2"><b><a href="#ref_n2">^</a></b></span>  Anguilla was completely separated from Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla in 1980 and remaining Saint Kitts and Nevis became independent from the United Kingdom in 1983.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n3"><b><a href="#ref_n3">^</a></b></span>  British Guiana was renamed Guyana in 1966.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n4"><b><a href="#ref_n4">^</a></b></span>  British Honduras was renamed Belize in 1973.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n5"><b><a href="#ref_n5">^</a></b></span>  Ceylon was renamed Sri Lanka in 1972.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n6"><b><a href="#ref_n6">^</a></b></span>  Fiji was re-suspended from the Commonwealth and Games in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-NZ_Herald_10594683_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NZ_Herald_10594683-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Fiji\'s suspension from the Commonwealth was lifted in time for the 2014 Games following <a href="/wiki/Fijian_general_election,_2014" title="Fijian general election, 2014">democratic elections</a> in March, 2014.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n7"><b><a href="#ref_n7">^</a></b></span>  The Gambia withdrew from the Commonwealth in 2013, but rejoined on 8 February 2018; The Gambia was readmitted to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">Commonwealth Games Federation</a> in March 2018.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n8"><b><a href="#ref_n8">^</a></b></span>  Gold Coast (British colony) was renamed Ghana in 1957.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n9"><b><a href="#ref_n9">^</a></b></span>  Including neighbouring Islands.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n10"><b><a href="#ref_n10">^</a></b></span>  Hong Kong was never a Commonwealth member but was a territory of a Commonwealth country; it ceased to be in the Commonwealth when the territory was <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_of_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer of sovereignty of Hong Kong">handed over</a> to China in 1997.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n11"><b><a href="#ref_n11">^</a></b></span>  Ireland was represented as a single team from the whole of the <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">island</a> in 1930, and by two teams, representing the Irish Free State, and Northern Ireland in 1934. The Irish Free State was officially renamed <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">\xc3\x89ire</a> in 1937 but did not participate in the 1938 Games, and withdrew from the Commonwealth when it unilaterally declared that it was the Republic of Ireland on 18 April 1948.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n12"><b><a href="#ref_n12">^</a></b></span>  Contemporary illustrations show Green Flag used for the Irish team.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n13"><b><a href="#ref_n13">^</a></b></span>  Malawi, Zambia and Zimbabwe competed in 1962 as part of Rhodesia and Nyasaland.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n14"><b><a href="#ref_n14">^</a></b></span>  Malaya, North Borneo, Sarawak and Singapore federated as Malaysia in 1963. Singapore left the federation in 1965.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n15"><b><a href="#ref_n15">^</a></b></span>  The Maldives withdrew from the Commonwealth in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n16"><b><a href="#ref_n16">^</a></b></span>  Newfoundland joined Canada in 1949.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n17"><b><a href="#ref_n17">^</a></b></span>  The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Banner" title="Ulster Banner">Ulster Banner</a> was the flag of the former Government of Northern Ireland only between 1953 and 1972, but the flag has been regarded as flag of Northern Ireland since 1924 among <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">unionists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster_loyalism" title="Ulster loyalism">loyalists</a>. The Ulster Banner is the sporting flag of Northern Ireland in other events as the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_World_Championship_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="FIVB Volleyball World Championship (disambiguation)">FIVB Volleyball World Championship</a>.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n18"><b><a href="#ref_n18">^</a></b></span>  Southern Rhodesia and Northern Rhodesia federated with Nyasaland in 1953 as <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Rhodesia_and_Nyasaland" title="Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland">Rhodesia and Nyasaland</a>, which dissolved at the end of 1963.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n19"><b><a href="#ref_n19">^</a></b></span>  Southern Rhodesia and Northern Rhodesia competed separately in 1954 and 1958 while both were part of the Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n20"><b><a href="#ref_n20">^</a></b></span>  Under the name of "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a>" in the Commonwealth Games.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">Tristan da Cunha</a> were dependencies of Saint Helena, so the territory was officially called "Saint Helena and Dependencies" until 2009. Saint Helena, Ascension Island and Tristan da Cunha became equal parts of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a> in 2009.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n21"><b><a href="#ref_n21">^</a></b></span>  Western Samoa was renamed Samoa in 1997.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n22"><b><a href="#ref_n22">^</a></b></span>  Zanzibar and Tanganyika federated to form Tanzania in 1964.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n23"><b><a href="#ref_n23">^</a></b></span>  Zimbabwe withdrew from the Commonwealth in 2003.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n24"><b><a href="#ref_n24">^</a></b></span>  United Kingdom were the host of the Inter-Empire Championships in 1911. This event was held before the 1st edition of the Games held in Hamilton, Canada in 1930.</li></ol>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_nations_yet_to_send_teams">Commonwealth nations yet to send teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Commonwealth nations yet to send teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Very few Commonwealth dependencies and nations have yet to take part:<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">Tristan da Cunha</a>, former dependencies of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a> and current parts of the British Overseas Territory of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a>, have never formed their own teams independent from the Saint Helena team.</li>\n<li>Other states, territories and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous region">territorial autonomies</a> with native populations within the Commonwealth that may be eligible include <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Island" title="Christmas Island">Christmas Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">Cocos (Keeling) Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">territories</a> of Australia), <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> (a federal entity of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Federation of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>), <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> (<a href="/wiki/Outer_islands_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="Outer islands of Mauritius">outer islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> (a semi-autonomous part of Tanzania).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, represented by the Cornwall Commonwealth Games Association (CCGA), sent a bid for participation in the 2006 Commonwealth Games, however, their application was rejected by the CGF, who stated that the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_status_of_Cornwall" title="Constitutional status of Cornwall">constitutional status of Cornwall</a> was not an issue that should be resolved through this medium. However, in 2010, the CCGA sought to launch a legal challenge to the decision of the CGF, stating that the Cornish bid of 2006 fulfilled the entire criterion of the CGF, and by rejecting the bid, the CGF had violated their own code, failing to follow their own criteria for participation. The Cornwall team will therefore seek competition in the 2014 games.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> currently has no permanent population although there is a sizeable <a href="/wiki/Chagossian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagossian">population</a> who were <i>born</i> in the BIOT but currently live in <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and the United Kingdom and so would be eligible to compete on birth criteria.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus</a> has made applications to the CGF to send teams.</li>\n<li>It is also conceivable that any future members of the Commonwealth such as <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations#Applicants" title="Commonwealth of Nations">applicants</a> (for example <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>) may participate in future games. The <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Aden" title="Colony of Aden">Colony of Aden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_South_Arabia" title="Federation of South Arabia">Federation of South Arabia</a>, precursors to modern Yemen, participated before in <a href="/wiki/1962_Commonwealth_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="1962 Commonwealth Games">1962</a> and in <a href="/wiki/1966_Commonwealth_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="1966 Commonwealth Games">1966</a>. Sudan was an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">Anglo-Egyptian protectorate</a> until independence in 1956.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">Pitcairn Islands</a>\' tiny population (currently 50 to 60 people) would appear to prevent this British overseas territory from competing.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">Tokelau</a> was <a href="/wiki/Tokelau_at_the_Commonwealth_Games" title="Tokelau at the Commonwealth Games">expected to take part</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010</a> Games in Delhi but did not do so.</li>\n<li>The lack of a permanent population would seem to prevent the British overseas territories of <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">British Antarctic Territory</a>, the New Zealand territory of <a href="/wiki/Ross_Dependency" title="Ross Dependency">Ross Dependency</a> and the Australian external territories of <a href="/wiki/Australian_Antarctic_Territory" title="Australian Antarctic Territory">Australian Antarctic Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashmore_and_Cartier_Islands" title="Ashmore and Cartier Islands">Ashmore and Cartier Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sea_Islands" title="Coral Sea Islands">Coral Sea Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heard_Island_and_McDonald_Islands" title="Heard Island and McDonald Islands">Heard Island and McDonald Islands</a> from competing.</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_city_contract">Host city contract</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Host city contract">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1934_British_Empire_Games" title="1934 British Empire Games">1934 British Empire Games</a>, originally awarded in 1930 to <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> was moved to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> after South Africa\'s pre-apartheid government refused to allow nonwhite participants.<sup id="cite_ref-Gorman2012_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gorman2012-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2022_Commonwealth_Games" title="2022 Commonwealth Games">2022 Commonwealth Games</a> were originally awarded to <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> on 2 September 2015, at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games_Federation" title="Commonwealth Games Federation">CGF</a> General Assembly in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> It was reported in February 2017 that Durban may be unable to host the games due to financial constraints. On 13 March 2017, the CGF stripped Durban of their rights to host and reopened the bidding process for the 2022 games.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Many cities from Australia, Canada, England and Malaysia expressed interest to host the games. However, the CGF received only one official bid and that was from <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, England.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 21 December 2017, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> was awarded for the 2022 Games as Durban\'s replacement host.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boycotts">Boycotts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Boycotts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> boycotted the <a href="/wiki/1978_Commonwealth_Games" title="1978 Commonwealth Games">1978 Commonwealth Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a> in protest of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>\'s sporting contacts with <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>-era <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> also stayed away, in protest of alleged Canadian hostility towards the government of <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">Idi Amin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MacintoshHawes1994_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacintoshHawes1994-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Edmonton_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edmonton-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1986_Commonwealth_Games_(Edinburgh)_boycotting_countries_(red).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png/300px-1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png" width="300" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png/450px-1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png/600px-1986_Commonwealth_Games_%28Edinburgh%29_boycotting_countries_%28red%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1986_Commonwealth_Games_(Edinburgh)_boycotting_countries_(red).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries boycotting the 1986 Games are shaded red</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/1986_Commonwealth_Games" title="1986 Commonwealth Games">1986 Commonwealth Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, a majority of the Commonwealth nations staged a boycott, so that the Games appeared to be a whites-only event. Thirty two of the eligible fifty nine countries\xe2\x80\x94largely African, Asian and Caribbean states\xe2\x80\x94stayed away because of the <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Thatcher</a> government\'s policy of keeping Britain\'s sporting links with <a href="/wiki/Apartheid_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Apartheid South Africa">apartheid South Africa</a> in preference to participating in the general sporting boycott of that country. Consequently, Edinburgh 1986 witnessed the lowest number of athletes since Auckland 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The boycotting nations were <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">Gambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">St. Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">St. Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda was a particularly late withdrawal, as its athletes appeared in the opening ceremony and in the opening day of competition before the Bermuda Olympic Association decided to formally withdraw.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The estimated cost of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> were US$11 billion, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Today_(India)" title="Business Today (India)">Business Today</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The initial total budget estimated by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Olympic_Association" title="Indian Olympic Association">Indian Olympic Association</a> in 2003 was US$250 million. In 2010, however, the official total budget soon escalated to an estimated US$1.8 billion, a figure which excluded non-sports-related infrastructure development.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The 2010 Commonwealth Games are reportedly the most expensive Commonwealth Games ever.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_competitors">Notable competitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notable competitors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Lawn bowler <a href="/wiki/Willie_Wood_(bowler)" title="Willie Wood (bowler)">Willie Wood</a> from <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> was the first competitor to have competed in seven Commonwealth Games, from 1974 to 2002, a record equalled in 2014 by <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> cyclist Andrew Roche.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>They have both been surpassed by David Calvert of Northern Ireland who in 2018 attended his 11th games.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Greg_Yelavich" title="Greg Yelavich">Greg Yelavich</a>, a sports shooter from New Zealand, has won 12 medals in seven games from 1986 to 2010.\n</p><p>Lawn Bowler <a href="/wiki/Robert_Weale" title="Robert Weale">Robert Weale</a> has represented Wales in 8 Commonwealth Games, 1986\xe2\x80\x932014, winning 2 gold, 3 silver and 1 bronze.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauruan</a> weightlifter <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Stephen" title="Marcus Stephen">Marcus Stephen</a> won twelve medals at the Games between 1990 and 2002, of which seven gold, and was elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nauru" title="President of Nauru">President of Nauru</a> in 2007. His performance has helped place Nauru (the smallest independent state in the Commonwealth, at 21&#160;km<sup>2</sup> and with a population of fewer than 9,400 in 2011) in nineteenth place on the <a href="/wiki/All-time_Commonwealth_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Commonwealth Games medal table">all-time Commonwealth Games medal table</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ian_Thorpe" title="Ian Thorpe">Ian Thorpe</a>, Australian swimmer (now retired), has won 10 Commonwealth Games gold medals and 1 silver medal. At the <a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, he won 4 gold medals. At the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, he won 6 gold medals and 1 silver medal.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chad_le_Clos" title="Chad le Clos">Chad le Clos</a>, South Africa\xe2\x80\x99s most decorated swimmer, has won 17 medals from just three Commonwealth Games (<a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018</a>), seven of which are gold. At the <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018 Commonwealth Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, he won three golds, a silver and a bronze.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span
